Section 1:
2025 Session (83rd) A AB534 909
Amendment No. 909
Proposed by: Assemblymember Monroe-Moreno
Amends: Summary: No Title: Yes Preamble: No Joint Sponsorship: No Digest: Yes
Adoption of this amendment will MAINTAIN the unfunded mandate not requested by the affected local government to
A.B. 534 (§§ 18, 20, 51, 61).
ASSEMBLY ACTION Initial and Date | SENATE ACTION Initial and Date
Adopted Lost | Adopted Lost
Concurred In Not | Concurred In Not
Receded Not | Receded Not
EXPLANATION: Matter in (1) blue bold italics is new language in the original
bill; (2) variations of green bold underlining is language proposed to be added in
this amendment; (3) red strikethrough is deleted language in the original bill; (4)
purple double strikethrough is language proposed to be deleted in this amendment;
(5) orange double underlining is deleted language in the original bill proposed to be
retained in this amendment.
-
KMD/HAC Date: 5/29/2025
A.B. No. 534—Revises provisions relating to elections. (BDR 24-975)
*A_AB534_909*
Page 1 of 49
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 3
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 534–COMMITTEE ON
LEGISLATIVE OPERATIONS AND ELECTIONS
(ON BEHALF OF THE SECRETARY OF STATE)
MARCH 24, 2025
_______________
Referred to Committee on Legislative Operations and Elections
SUMMARY—Revises provisions relating to elections. (BDR 24-975)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Yes.
CONTAINS UNFUNDED MANDATE (§§ [2,] 18, 20, [21,] 51, 61)
(NOT REQUESTED BY AFFECTED LOCAL GOVERNMENT)
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to elections; [requiring the Secretary of State to allow certain
persons detained in jail to use the system of approved electronic
transmission to register to vote and cast a ballot;] revising provisions
relating to voter registration and updating voter registration
information; renaming certain provisional ballots to “conditional
ballots”; revising provisions relating to certain petitions; [revising the
deadline for candidates to file a declaration of candidacy;] revising
provisions relating to the publication of certain information by a
county clerk; [authorizing the Secretary of State to require certain
employees to attend a training course concerning elections
procedures;] revising provisions relating mail ballots; revising
provisions relating to the testing of certain technology prior to an
election; defining the term “personal knowledge” for purposes of
certain challenges; revising provisions relating to risk-limiting audits;
revising provisions relating to certain prohibited conduct in or around a
polling place; revising provisions relating to mechanical voting
systems; authorizing, under certain circumstances, the Secretary of
State to adjust the date of the presidential preference primary election;
making various other changes relating to elections; and providing other
matters properly relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 [Existing law requires the Secretary of State to establish a system of approved electronic
2 transmission through which voters may register to vote and apply for and cast a ballot. (NRS
3 293D.200) Existing law further sets forth provisions governing voting by persons who are
4 detained in a county or city jail. (NRS 293.269971, 293.269973, 293.269975) Section 2 of this
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 4
5 bill requires the Secretary of State to allow: (1) an elector who is detained in a county or city
6 jail to use the system of approved electronic transmission established for covered voters who
7 are overseas or in the military to register to vote; and (2) a registered voter who is detained in
8 a county or city jail to use the system of approved electronic transmission to apply for and cast
9 a ballot in every election where the system of approved electronic transmission is available to
10 a covered voter who is overseas or in the military. Section 15 of this bill requires the Secretary
11 of State to prescribe the procedures to be followed and the requirements of the use of the
12 system of approved electronic transmission by electors and voters who are detained in a
13 county or city jail. Section 21 of this bill requires the report submitted to the Secretary of State
14 by a person who administers a county or city jail concerning elections conducted in such jails
15 to include an explanation of the process the jail used to comply with the provisions of section
16 2. (NRS 293.269975)]
17 Section 3 of this bill requires, with limited exception, a county or city clerk to respond
18 within 2 working days after receiving any request from the Secretary of State for information
19 or data relating to [an] the current election [.] cycle.
20 Section 4 of this bill provides that if an active registered voter moves to another county
21 and registers to vote therein, which may include, without limitation, an application to register
22 to vote which is transmitted to a county clerk from an automatic voter registration agency, it
23 shall be deemed that the voter is updating his or her voter registration rather than registering to
24 vote and, with certain exceptions, the voter must not be required to cast a provisional ballot on
25 the basis of such an update.
26 Existing law sets forth certain procedures governing the use of provisional ballots by
27 registered voters who update their voter registration information after the close of registration
28 for an election and by electors who register to vote in person or by computer during certain
29 periods of time leading up to and during an election. Specifically, existing law: (1) with
30 certain exceptions, requires an elector who is deemed conditionally registered to vote under
31 such circumstances to cast his or her vote by a provisional ballot; and (2) authorizes a county
32 or city clerk, under certain circumstances, to require a registered voter who updates his or her
33 voter registration to cast a provisional ballot in an election. (NRS 293.5772-293.5887)
34 Sections 5, 23, 26, 32 and 38-47 of this bill rename ballots cast under such circumstances to
35 be “conditional ballots.”
36 Existing law requires certain petitions to be submitted to a county clerk for verification of
37 the signatures on the petition and sets forth certain deadlines for such submission. (NRS
38 293.128, 293.172, 293.200, 295.056, 298.109, 306.035, 306.110) Section 65 of this bill
39 [prohibits] authorizes a county clerk, under certain circumstances, to delay beginning
40 verification for petitions for referendum and certain initiatives . [from being submitted to a
41 county clerk earlier than the 13th day following the primary or general election, as
42 appropriate.] (NRS 295.056) Existing law requires, after the submission of certain petitions
43 containing signatures which are required to be verified, the county clerk to determine the
44 number of signatures affixed to the documents and forward that information to the Secretary
45 of State. (NRS 293.1276) Section 6 of this bill increases the time provided to a county clerk to
46 make such a determination: (1) for a petition to place the name of a candidate for partisan
47 office of a minor political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the ballot,
48 from 2 working days to 7 working days; and (2) for any other petition which is required to be
49 submitted for such purposes, from 4 working days to 9 working days.
50 If the Secretary of State finds that the total number of signatures submitted to all the
51 county clerks is 100 percent or more of the number of registered voters needed to declare the
52 petition sufficient, existing law requires: (1) the Secretary of State to immediately notify the
53 county clerks; and (2) each of the county clerks, after the receipt of such notification, to
54 determine the number of registered voters who have signed the document. (NRS 293.1277)
55 Section 7 of this bill increases the time provided to a county clerk to make such a
56 determination: (1) for a petition to recall a public officer who holds a statewide office, from
57 20 working days to 25 working days; (2) for a petition to place the name of a candidate for
58 partisan office of a minor political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the
59 ballot, from 3 working days to 8 working days; and (3) for any other petition which is required
60 to be submitted for such purposes, from 9 working days to 14 working days. Sections 8 and
61 11 of this bill require a petition to place the name of a candidate for partisan office of a minor
62 political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the ballot be submitted to the
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 5
63 county clerk for verification or filing, respectively, not later than 25 working days, rather
64 than 10 working days, before the last day to file the petition.
65 Existing law [provides] requires that the [period for filing a declaration] petition of
66 candidacy [: (1) for judicial candidates begins on the first Monday in January of the year in
67 which the election is to be held and ends the second Friday after the first Monday in January;
68 and (2) for all nonjudicial candidates begins on] for an independent candidate for partisan
69 office be filed not earlier than the first Monday in March of the year in which the election is
70 to be held and [ends] not later than the [second] third Friday [after the first Monday] in
71 [March. (NRS 293.177, 293C.145, 293C.175) Sections 9-11, 58 and 59 of this bill instead
72 provide that the period for filing a declaration of candidacy for both judicial and nonjudicial
73 candidates begins on the first Monday in February of the year in which the election is to be
74 held and ends not later than 5 p.m. on the second Friday after the first Monday in February.
75 Section 9 similarly revises the dates by which a minor political party is required by existing
76 law to file a list of its candidates for partisan office. (NRS 293.1725)] June. (NRS 293.200)
77 Section 11 [further] instead provides that a petition of candidacy for an independent
78 candidate for partisan office must not be filed earlier than the [first] second Monday [in
79 February rather] after the primary election and not later than the [first Monday in March.]
80 third Friday after the primary election. Section 11 additionally: (1) requires such a
81 petition to be submitted to the county clerk for verification during this period of time;
82 and (2) provides that if such a petition is submitted in a timely manner but the Secretary
83 of State receives certificates from the county clerks showing the petition has met certain
84 requirements after this deadline, the petition is deemed to be timely filed.
85 Existing law requires a county clerk to publish certain information concerning elections
86 in a newspaper of general circulation. (NRS 293.203, 293.253, 293.3073, 293.3576, 293.391,
87 293.464, 298.670) Sections 12, 25, 27, 28, 31 and 68 of this bill instead require the county
88 clerk to publish such notices in such a manner as the county clerk deems proper, which may
89 include, without limitation, publication in a newspaper of general circulation, on the Internet
90 website of the county clerk or on the social media account of the county clerk.
91 Under existing law, the Secretary of State is required to cause to be published in a
92 newspaper of general circulation, on three separate occasions, in each county of the State,
93 together with any explanatory matter to be placed on the ballot, the entire text of a proposed
94 amendment to the Nevada Constitution which is proposed by an initiative petition. (Nev. Art.
95 19, § 2; NRS 293.253) Section 17 of this bill authorizes a county clerk to also publish such
96 materials in any other manner as the county clerk deems proper which may include, without
97 limitation, publication on the Internet website of the county clerk or on the social media
98 account of the county clerk.
99 Existing law requires the Secretary of State to adopt regulations, not inconsistent with the
100 election laws of this State, for the conduct of primary, presidential preference primary,
101 general, special and district elections in all cities and counties. (NRS 293.247) Section 14 of
102 this bill authorizes the Secretary of State to adopt regulations which provide standards for
103 certain reports which are required to be filed by a county or city clerk.
104 [Section 16 of this bill authorizes the Secretary of State to require any deputy or
105 employee of the Office of the Secretary of State whose duties relate to elections to attend the
106 training course provided by the Secretary of State concerning elections procedures. (NRS
107 293.2504)]
108 Existing law authorizes a mail ballot central counting board to begin counting the
109 received mail ballots 15 days before the day of the election and requires the board to complete
110 the count of all mail ballots on or before the seventh day following the election. (NRS
111 293.269931, 293C.26331) Sections 20 and 61 of this bill: (1) require, instead of authorize, the
112 mail ballot central counting board to begin counting the received mail ballots 15 days before
113 the day of the election; and (2) require the mail ballot central counting board to process each
114 mail ballot [on] within 24 hours after receipt of the [day that the] mail ballot unless a
115 waiver is [received. Section] granted by the Secretary of State. Sections 19 and 60 of this
116 bill [requires] require the Secretary of State, rather than a county or city clerk, to establish
117 procedures for minimum requirements for the processing and counting of mail ballots.
118 (NRS [293.269925)] 293.269925, 293C.26325)
119 Existing law requires a county clerk to: (1) prepare and distribute to certain persons in the
120 county a mail ballot for every election; and (2) allow a voter to elect not to receive such a mail
121 ballot by submitting a written notice to the county clerk which must be received by the county
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 6
122 clerk not later than 60 days before the day of the election. (NRS 293.269911) Section 18 of
123 this bill authorizes a voter who elects not to receive a mail ballot to later elect to receive a
124 mail ballot for the election if he or she, not later than 14 days before the election, submits to
125 the county clerk a written notice in the form prescribed by the county clerk. Sections 18 and
126 59.5 of this bill revise the deadline for distributing a mail ballot to each registered voter
127 who resides within the State from not later than 20 days before the election to instead on
128 or after the fifth Monday before the election but not later than the fourth Monday
129 before the election.
130 Existing law authorizes an elector to vote in the county or city in which the elector is
131 eligible to vote by submitting an application to register to vote by computer using the system
132 established by the Secretary of State before the elector appears at a polling place to vote in
133 person. Existing law further requires an elector who submits an application to register to vote
134 in such a manner less than 14 days before the election to vote in person. (NRS 293.5837,
135 293.671) Section 41 of this bill instead requires an elector who submits such an application
136 less than 18 days before the election to vote in person. Section 18 requires a county clerk to
137 prepare and distribute a mail ballot to each person who registers to vote or updates his or her
138 voter registration information not later than 18 days, rather than 14 days, before the election.
139 (NRS 293.269911)
140 Existing law requires a county clerk, if the county clerk uses an electronic roster, to
141 complete a test of the electronic roster not earlier than 2 weeks before and not later than 5 p.m.
142 on the day before the first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance to ensure
143 its functionality. (NRS 293.275) Section 22 of this bill prohibits such a test from being
144 completed earlier than 6 weeks, instead of 2 weeks, before the first day of the period for early
145 voting by personal appearance. Section 55 of this bill similarly revises the time period
146 provided in existing law for a county or city clerk to perform certain tests on a mechanical
147 recording device which directly records votes electronically and any automatic tabulating
148 equipment and programs. (NRS 293B.150)
149 Sections 24 and 33 of this bill define the term “personal knowledge” for purposes of
150 certain provisions of existing law which authorize certain persons to challenge the right of a
151 person to vote and provide that the term does not include knowledge obtained from a third
152 party. (NRS 293.303, 293.535)
153 Existing law requires each county clerk to conduct a risk-limiting audit of the results of
154 an election. (NRS 293.394) Section 29 of this bill renames such audits to “election accuracy
155 audits.” Existing law provides that certain materials used in the completion of logic and
156 accuracy tests must be sealed and deposited in the vaults of the county clerk. (NRS 293B.170)
157 Section 56 of this bill provides that such materials are subject to inspection for the purposes of
158 an election accuracy audit.
159 Section 30 of this bill provides that the term “canvass” as used in certain provisions
160 relating to recounts demanded by a candidate defeated at an election includes, in any general
161 election, the canvass by the Supreme Court of the returns for a candidate for United States
162 Senator or Representative in Congress. (NRS 293.403)
163 Existing law requires a county clerk to cancel the preregistration or registration of a
164 person under certain circumstances and authorizes or requires the reregistration of certain
165 electors whose registration is cancelled. (NRS 293.540, 293.543) Section 34 of this bill
166 requires a county clerk to cancel the preregistration or registration of a person if the county
167 clerk receives, from a person who is within the second degree of consanguinity of the person,
168 a sworn affidavit which indicates the death of the person. Section 35 of this bill requires, if
169 the registration or preregistration of an elector is cancelled under such circumstances and the
170 county clerk later determines that the registration or preregistration should not have been
171 cancelled, the county clerk to reregister or repreregister the elector.
172 Existing law provides that the last day for a person to register to vote for certain elections
173 that are held on the same day as a primary election, presidential preference primary election or
174 general election is, if the person is registering by appearing in person at the office of the
175 county clerk or certain county facilities, the fourth Tuesday preceding the primary election,
176 presidential preference primary election or general election. (NRS 293.560) Section 36 of this
177 bill instead provides that the last day to register to vote in such a manner is the day before the
178 first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance. Section 62 of this bill similarly
179 revises such deadlines for registration for a primary city, general city, recall and special city
180 election if there is a period for early voting for the primary or general city election. Section 37
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 7
181 of this bill requires, if an application to register to vote is received not later than 5 days after
182 the appropriate deadline, a county clerk to accept the application if it is obtained from the
183 Department of Motor Vehicles and is completed by, depending on if there is a period for early
184 voting by personal appearance, the day before the first day of the period for early voting by
185 personal appearance or the last day to register to vote by mail. (NRS 293.5727)
186 Existing law further provides that if a recall or special election is not held on the same
187 day as certain elections, the last day to register to vote for the recall or special election by any
188 method of registration is the third Saturday preceding the recall or special election. (NRS
189 293.560) Section 36 instead provides that the last day to register to vote for such a recall or
190 special election: (1) by mail is the second Tuesday preceding the recall or special election; (2)
191 by appearing in person at the office of the county clerk or certain county facilities is,
192 depending on if there is a period for early voting for the recall or special election, either the
193 day before the first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance or the third
194 Saturday preceding the recall or special election; and (3) by computer using the system
195 established on the Internet website of the Office of the Secretary of State is the day of the
196 recall or special election. Section 62 similarly revises deadlines for such registration for such
197 recall and special city elections.
198 Sections 48 and 49 of this bill exempt a person who is conducting an exit poll from
199 certain provisions of law which prohibit a person from: (1) with certain exceptions, remaining
200 inside or outside of any polling place so as to interfere with the conduct of an election; and (2)
201 in certain locations, soliciting a vote or speaking to a voter on the subject of marking the
202 voter’s ballots. (NRS 293.730, 293.740)
203 Section 50 of this bill provides that the termination of a contract by certain local
204 governing bodies for the lease or use of a mechanical voting system or mechanical recording
205 device which is currently used in any election of this State is provisional unless such an entity:
206 (1) submits to the Secretary of State a plan to transition to a new mechanical voting system or
207 mechanical recording device which is approved by the Secretary of State; and (2) signs a
208 contract for the purchase, lease or use of the new mechanical voting system or mechanical
209 recording device.
210 Existing law authorizes mechanical voting systems to be used to cast, register, record and
211 count ballots or votes at all statewide, county, city and district elections of any kind held in
212 this State. (NRS 293B.050) Section 51 of this bill instead provides that ballots or votes: (1)
213 may be cast, registered and recorded using a mechanical voting system; and (2) must be
214 counted using a mechanical voting system. Sections 13, 52-54, 57, 63, 64, 66 and 69-80 of
215 this bill make conforming changes to require the use of a mechanical voting system for
216 counting votes and clarify that the use of a mechanical voting system for casting ballots is
217 authorized but not required.
218 Section 67 of this bill authorizes the Secretary of State, with the approval of the
219 Legislative Commission, to adjust the date of the presidential primary election which is set
220 forth in existing law as the first Tuesday in February of each presidential election year. (NRS
221 298.650)
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:

4 completed within [9] 14 days, excluding Saturdays, Sundays and holidays, after the

14 signatures any signature included in the incorrect petition district.
15 2. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 3 and 4, if more than 500
16 names have been signed on the documents submitted to a county clerk, the county
17 clerk shall examine the signatures by sampling them at random for verification. The
18 random sample of signatures to be verified must be drawn in such a manner that
19 every signature which has been submitted to the county clerk is given an equal
20 opportunity to be included in the sample. The sample must include an examination
21 of:
22 (a) Except as otherwise provided in paragraph (b), at least 500 or 5 percent of
23 the signatures, whichever is greater.
24 (b) If the petition is for the recall of a public officer who holds a statewide
25 office, at least 25 percent of the signatures.
26  If documents were submitted to the county clerk for more than one petition
27 district wholly contained within that county, a separate random sample must be
28 performed for each petition district.
29 3. If a petition district comprises more than one county and the petition is for
30 an initiative or referendum proposing a constitutional amendment or a statewide
31 measure, and if more than 500 names have been signed on the documents submitted
32 for that petition district, the appropriate county clerks shall examine the signatures
33 by sampling them at random for verification. The random sample of signatures to
34 be verified must be drawn in such a manner that every signature which has been
35 submitted to the county clerks within the petition district is given an equal
36 opportunity to be included in the sample. The sample must include an examination
37 of at least 500 or 5 percent of the signatures presented in the petition district,
38 whichever is greater. The Secretary of State shall determine the number of
39 signatures that must be verified by each county clerk within the petition district.
40 4. If a petition is for the recall of a public officer who does not hold a
41 statewide office, each county clerk:
42 (a) Shall not examine the signatures by sampling them at random for
43 verification;
44 (b) Shall examine for verification every signature on the documents submitted
45 to the county clerk; and
46 (c) When determining the total number of valid signatures on the documents,
47 shall remove each name of a registered voter who submitted a request to have his or
48 her name removed from the petition pursuant to NRS 306.015.
49 5. In determining from the records of registration the number of registered
50 voters who signed the documents, the county clerk may use the signatures
51 contained in the file of applications to register to vote. If the county clerk uses that
52 file, the county clerk shall ensure that every application in the file is examined,
53 including any application in his or her possession which may not yet be entered into

1 the county clerk’s records. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 6, the county
2 clerk shall rely only on the appearance of the signature and the address and date
3 included with each signature in making his or her determination.

6 State pursuant to NRS 293.671;
7 (b) A person registers to vote pursuant to NRS 293D.230 and signs his or her
8 application to register to vote using a digital signature or an electronic signature; or
9 (c) A person is registered to vote by an automatic voter registration agency,
10  the county clerk may rely on such other indicia as prescribed by the Secretary of
11 State in making his or her determination.

1 Sec. 17. NRS 293.253 is hereby amended to read as follows:
2 293.253 1. The Secretary of State shall provide each county clerk with
3 copies of any proposed constitution or constitutional amendment which will appear
4 on the general election ballot, together with the copies of the condensations,
5 explanations, arguments, rebuttals and fiscal notes prepared pursuant to NRS
6 218D.810, 293.250 and 293.252.
7 2. Whenever feasible, the Secretary of State shall provide those copies on or
8 before the first Monday in August of the year in which the proposals will appear on
9 the ballot. Copies of any additional proposals must be provided as soon after their
10 filing as feasible.
11 3. Each county clerk shall cause a copy of the full text of any such
12 constitution or amendment and its condensation, explanation, arguments, rebuttals
13 and fiscal note to be published, in conspicuous display advertising format of not
14 less than 10 column inches, in a newspaper of general circulation in the county
15 three times at intervals of not less than 7 days, the first publication to be on or
16 before the first Monday in October. If no such newspaper is published in the
17 county, the publication may be made in a newspaper of general circulation
18 published in the nearest Nevada county [.] and in addition to any publication made
19 in a newspaper pursuant to this subsection, a county clerk may publish a copy of
20 the full text of any such constitution or amendment and its condensation,
21 explanation, arguments, rebuttals and fiscal note in such a manner as the county
22 clerk deems proper which may include, without limitation, publication on the
23 Internet website of the county clerk or on the social media account of the county
24 clerk.
25 4. If a copy of any such constitution or amendment is furnished by the
26 Secretary of State too late to be published at 7-day intervals, it must be published
27 three times at the longest intervals feasible in each county.
28 5. The portion of the cost of publication which is attributable to publishing the
29 questions, explanations, arguments, rebuttals and fiscal notes of proposed
30 constitutions or constitutional amendments is a charge against the State and must be
31 paid from the Reserve for Statutory Contingency Account upon recommendation by
32 the Secretary of State and approval by the State Board of Examiners.
33 Sec. 18. NRS 293.269911 is hereby amended to read as follows:
34 293.269911 1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, the county clerk
35 shall prepare and distribute to each active registered voter in the county and each
36 person who registers to vote or updates his or her voter registration information not
37 later than the [14] 18 days before the election a mail ballot for every election. The
38 county clerk shall make reasonable accommodations for the use of the mail ballot
39 by a person who is elderly or disabled, including, without limitation, by providing,
40 upon request, the mail ballot in 12-point type to a person who is elderly or disabled.
41 2. The county clerk shall allow a voter to elect not to receive a mail ballot
42 pursuant to this section by submitting to the county clerk a written notice in the
43 form prescribed by the county clerk which must be received by the county clerk not
44 later than 60 days before the day of the election. If a voter elects not to receive a
45 mail ballot pursuant to this subsection, he or she may later elect to receive a mail
46 ballot for the election if he or she, not later than 14 days before the election,
47 submits to the county clerk a written notice in the form prescribed by the county
48 clerk.
49 3. The county clerk shall not distribute a mail ballot to any person who:
50 (a) Registers to vote for the election pursuant to the provisions of NRS
51 293.5772 to 293.5887, inclusive; or
52 (b) Elects not to receive a mail ballot pursuant to subsection 2.

1 4. The mail ballot must include all offices, candidates and measures upon
2 which the voter is entitled to vote at the election.
3 5. Except as otherwise provided in subsections 2 and 3, the mail ballot must
4 be distributed to:
5 (a) Each active registered voter who:
6 (1) Resides within the State, on or after the fifth Monday before the
7 election but not later than [20 days] the fourth Monday before the election; and
8 (2) Except as otherwise provided in paragraph (c), resides outside the
9 State, not later than 40 days before the election.
10 (b) Each active registered voter who registers to vote after the dates set for
11 distributing mail ballots pursuant to paragraph (a) but who is eligible to receive a
12 mail ballot pursuant to subsection 1, not later than 13 days before the election.
13 (c) Each covered voter who is entitled to have a military-overseas ballot
14 transmitted pursuant to the provisions of chapter 293D of NRS or the Uniformed
15 and Overseas Citizens Absentee Voting Act, 52 U.S.C. §§ 20301 et seq., not later
16 than the time required by those provisions.
17 6. In the case of a special election where no candidate for federal office will
18 appear on the ballot, the mail ballot must be distributed to each active registered
19 voter not later than 15 days before the special election.
20 7. Any untimely legal action which would prevent the mail ballot from being
21 distributed to any voter pursuant to this section is moot and of no effect.

31 Sec. 20. NRS 293.269931 is hereby amended to read as follows:
32 293.269931 1. The mail ballot central counting board [may] shall begin
33 counting the received mail ballots 15 days before the day of the election [.] and
34 must process each mail ballot pursuant to NRS 293.269933 [on the day that]
35 within 24 hours after the receipt of the mail ballot [is received.] unless the
36 Secretary of State grants a waiver requested pursuant to subsection 2. The board
37 must complete the count of all mail ballots on or before the seventh day following
38 the election. The counting procedure must be public.
39 2. If a mail ballot central counting board is unable to process a mail ballot
40 within 24 hours after the receipt of the mail ballot, the mail ballot central
41 counting board may request a waiver from the Secretary of State to extend the
42 time that the mail ballot central counting board has to process the mail ballot. A
43 waiver granted pursuant to this subsection must not authorize the mail ballot
44 central counting board to count the mail ballot after the deadline for the
45 completion of the count of all mail ballots set forth in subsection 1.
46 3. If two or more mail ballots are found folded together to present the
47 appearance of a single ballot, the mail ballots must be rejected and placed in an
48 envelope, upon which must be written the reason for their rejection. The envelope
49 must be signed by an election board officer and placed in the container or ballot
50 box after the count is completed.

44 Sec. 24. NRS 293.303 is hereby amended to read as follows:
45 293.303 1. A person applying to vote may be challenged:
46 (a) Orally by any registered voter of the precinct upon the ground that he or she
47 is not the person entitled to vote as claimed or has voted before at the same
48 election. A registered voter who initiates a challenge pursuant to this paragraph
49 must submit an affirmation that is signed under penalty of perjury and in the form
50 prescribed by the Secretary of State stating that the challenge is based on the
51 personal knowledge of the registered voter.
52 (b) On any ground set forth in a challenge filed with the county clerk pursuant
53 to the provisions of NRS 293.547.
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 24
1 2. If a person is challenged, an election board officer shall tender the
2 challenged person the following oath or affirmation:
3 (a) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person does not belong
4 to the political party designated upon the roster, “I swear or affirm under penalty of
5 perjury that I belong to the political party designated upon the roster”;
6 (b) If the challenge is on the ground that the roster does not show that the
7 challenged person designated the political party to which he or she claims to
8 belong, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I designated on the
9 application to register to vote the political party to which I claim to belong”;
10 (c) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person does not reside
11 at the residence for which the address is listed in the roster, “I swear or affirm under
12 penalty of perjury that I reside at the residence for which the address is listed in the
13 roster”;
14 (d) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person previously
15 voted a ballot for the election, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I
16 have not voted for any of the candidates or questions included on this ballot for this
17 election”; or
18 (e) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person is not the
19 person he or she claims to be, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I am
20 the person whose name is in this roster.”
21  The oath or affirmation must be set forth on a form prepared by the Secretary of
22 State and signed by the challenged person under penalty of perjury.
23 3. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 4, if the challenged person
24 refuses to execute the oath or affirmation so tendered, the person must not be issued
25 a ballot, and the election board officer shall indicate in the roster “Challenged” by
26 the person’s name.
27 4. If the challenged person refuses to execute the oath or affirmation set forth
28 in paragraph (a) or (b) of subsection 2, the election board officers shall issue the
29 person a nonpartisan ballot.
30 5. If the challenged person refuses to execute the oath or affirmation set forth
31 in paragraph (c) of subsection 2, the election board officers shall inform the person
32 that he or she is entitled to vote only in the manner prescribed in NRS 293.304.
33 6. If the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation and the challenge
34 is not based on the ground set forth in paragraph (e) of subsection 2, the election
35 board officers shall issue the person a partisan ballot.
36 7. If the challenge is based on the ground set forth in paragraph (c) of
37 subsection 2, and the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation, the
38 election board shall not issue the person a ballot until he or she furnishes
39 satisfactory identification which contains proof of the address at which the person
40 actually resides. For the purposes of this subsection, a voter registration card does
41 not provide proof of the address at which a person resides.
42 8. If the challenge is based on the ground set forth in paragraph (e) of
43 subsection 2 and the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation, the
44 election board shall not issue the person a ballot unless the person:
45 (a) Furnishes official identification which contains a photograph of the person,
46 such as a driver’s license or other official document; or
47 (b) Brings before the election board officers a person who is at least 18 years
48 of age who:
49 (1) Furnishes official identification which contains a photograph of that
50 person, such as a driver’s license or other official document; and
51 (2) Executes an oath or affirmation under penalty of perjury that the
52 challenged person is who he or she swears to be.
53 9. The election board officers shall:
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 25
1 (a) Record on the challenge list:
2 (1) The name of the challenged person;
3 (2) The name of the registered voter who initiated the challenge; and
4 (3) The result of the challenge; and
5 (b) If possible, orally notify the registered voter who initiated the challenge of
6 the result of the challenge.
7 10. For the purposes of this section, “personal knowledge” means firsthand
8 knowledge through experience or observation of the facts upon each ground that
9 the challenge is based. The term does not include knowledge obtained from a
10 third party, including, without limitation, information obtained from the review
11 of data in a database or other compilation of information.

13 Sec. 28. NRS 293.391 is hereby amended to read as follows:
14 293.391 1. The voted ballots, rejected ballots, spoiled ballots, challenge
15 lists, records printed on paper of voted ballots collected pursuant to NRS 293B.400,
16 reports prepared pursuant to NRS 293.269937 and stubs of the ballots used,
17 enclosed and sealed, must, after canvass of the votes by the board of county
18 commissioners, be deposited in the vaults of the county clerk. The records of voted
19 ballots that are maintained in electronic form must, after canvass of the votes by the
20 board of county commissioners, be sealed and deposited in the vaults of the county
21 clerk. The tally lists collected pursuant to this title must, after canvass of the votes
22 by the board of county commissioners, be deposited in the vaults of the county
23 clerk without being sealed. All materials described by this subsection must be
24 preserved for at least 22 months, and all such sealed materials must be destroyed
25 immediately after the preservation period. A notice of the destruction must , not
26 less than 2 weeks before the destruction, be published by the clerk in such a
27 manner as the county clerk deems proper which may include, without limitation,
28 publication in at least one newspaper of general circulation in the county [not less
29 than 2 weeks before] , on the Internet website of the county clerk or on the social
30 media account of the [destruction.] county clerk.
31 2. Unused ballots, enclosed and sealed, must, after canvass of the votes by the
32 board of county commissioners, be deposited in the vaults of the county clerk and
33 preserved for at least the period during which the election may be contested and
34 adjudicated, after which the unused ballots may be destroyed.
35 3. The rosters containing the signatures of those persons who voted in the
36 election and the tally lists deposited with the board of county commissioners are
37 subject to the inspection of any elector who may wish to examine them at any time
38 after their deposit with the county clerk.
39 4. A contestant of an election may inspect all of the material regarding that
40 election which is preserved pursuant to subsection 1 or 2, except the voted ballots
41 and records printed on paper of voted ballots collected pursuant to NRS 293B.400
42 which are deposited with the county clerk.
43 5. The voted ballots and records printed on paper of voted ballots collected
44 pursuant to NRS 293B.400 which are deposited with the county clerk are not
45 subject to the inspection of anyone, except in cases of a contested election, and then
46 only by the judge, body or board before whom the election is being contested, or by
47 the parties to the contest, jointly, pursuant to an order of such judge, body or board.

10 Sec. 30. NRS 293.403 is hereby amended to read as follows:
11 293.403 1. Except as otherwise provided in NRS 293.424, a candidate
12 defeated at any election may demand and receive a recount of the vote for the office
13 for which he or she is a candidate to determine the number of votes received for the
14 candidate and the number of votes received for the person who won the election if,
15 within 3 working days after the canvass of the vote and the certification by the
16 county clerk or city clerk of the abstract of votes, the candidate who demands the
17 recount:
18 (a) Files in writing a demand with the officer with whom the candidate filed his
19 or her declaration of candidacy; and
20 (b) Deposits in advance the estimated costs of the recount with that officer.
21 2. Any voter at an election may demand and receive a recount of the vote for
22 a ballot question if, within 3 working days after the canvass of the vote and the
23 certification by the county clerk or city clerk of the abstract of votes, the voter:
24 (a) Files in writing a demand with:
25 (1) The Secretary of State, if the demand is for a recount of a ballot
26 question affecting more than one county; or
27 (2) The county or city clerk who will conduct the recount, if the demand is
28 for a recount of a ballot question affecting only one county or city; and
29 (b) Deposits in advance the estimated costs of the recount with the person to
30 whom the demand was made.
31 3. The estimated costs of the recount must be determined by the person with
32 whom the advance is deposited based on regulations adopted by the Secretary of
33 State defining the term “costs.”
34 4. As used in this section, “canvass” means:
35 (a) In any primary election, the canvass by the board of county commissioners
36 of the returns for a candidate or ballot question voted for in one county or the
37 canvass by the board of county commissioners last completing its canvass of the
38 returns for a candidate or ballot question voted for in more than one county.
39 (b) In any primary city election, the canvass by the city council of the returns
40 for a candidate or ballot question voted for in the city.
41 (c) In any general election:
42 (1) The canvass by the Supreme Court of the returns for a candidate for
43 United States Senator, Representative in Congress or a statewide office or a
44 statewide ballot question; or
45 (2) The canvass of the board of county commissioners of the returns for
46 any other candidate or ballot question, as provided in paragraph (a).
47 (d) In any general city election, the canvass by the city council of the returns
48 for a candidate or ballot question voted for in the city.

12 Sec. 33. NRS 293.535 is hereby amended to read as follows:
13 293.535 1. The county clerk shall notify a registrant if any elector or other
14 reliable person files an affidavit with the county clerk stating that:
15 (a) The registrant is not a citizen of the United States; or
16 (b) The registrant has:
17 (1) Moved outside the boundaries of the county where he or she is
18 registered to another county, state, territory or foreign country, with the intention of
19 remaining there for an indefinite time and with the intention of abandoning his or
20 her residence in the county where registered; and
21 (2) Established residence in some other state, territory or foreign country,
22 or in some other county of this state, naming the place.
23  The affiant must state that he or she has personal knowledge of the facts set forth
24 in the affidavit.
25 2. Upon the filing of an affidavit pursuant to paragraph (b) of subsection 1,
26 the county clerk shall notify the registrant in the manner set forth in NRS 293.530
27 and shall enclose a copy of the affidavit. If the registrant fails to respond or appear
28 to vote within the required time, the county clerk shall cancel the registration.
29 3. An affidavit filed pursuant to paragraph (a) of subsection 1 must be filed
30 not later than 30 days before an election. Upon the filing of such an affidavit, the
31 county clerk shall notify the registrant by registered or certified mail, return receipt
32 requested, of the filing of the affidavit, and shall enclose a copy of the affidavit.
33 Unless the registrant, within 15 days after the return receipt has been filed in the
34 office of the county clerk, presents satisfactory proof of citizenship, the county
35 clerk shall cancel the registration.
36 4. The provisions of this section do not prevent the challenge provided for in
37 NRS 293.303 or 293C.292.
38 5. A county clerk is not required to take any action pursuant to this section in
39 relation to a person who is preregistered to vote until the person is deemed to be
40 registered to vote pursuant to subsection 2 of NRS 293.4855.
41 6. For the purposes of this section, “personal knowledge” means firsthand
42 knowledge through experience or observation of the facts upon each ground that
43 the challenge is based. The term does not include knowledge obtained from a
44 third party, including, without limitation, information obtained from the review
45 of data in a database or other compilation of information.

3 Sec. 48. NRS 293.730 is hereby amended to read as follows:
4 293.730 1. Except for an election board officer in the course of the election
5 board officer’s official duties, a person shall not:
6 (a) Remain in or outside of any polling place so as to interfere with the conduct
7 of the election. The provisions of this paragraph do not prohibit a person from
8 conducting an exit poll in or outside of the polling place.
9 (b) Accept from any voter a ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter, other
10 than a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter
11 with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
12 (c) Remove a ballot from any polling place before the closing of the polls.
13 (d) Apply for or receive a ballot at any election precinct or district other than
14 one at which the person is entitled to vote.
15 (e) Show his or her ballot to another person, after voting, so as to reveal any of
16 his or her votes on the ballot, other than on his or her mail ballot or military-
17 overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter with his or her authorization
18 pursuant to this title.
19 (f) Inside a polling place, ask another person for his or her name, address or
20 political affiliation or for whom he or she intends to vote.
21 (g) Send, transmit, distribute or deliver a ballot to a voter, other than a mail
22 ballot or military-overseas ballot when permitted pursuant to this title.
23 (h) Except when permitted by the voter, alter, change, deface, damage or
24 destroy a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the
25 voter with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
26 2. A voter shall not:
27 (a) Accept a ballot from another person, other than an election board officer in
28 the course of the election board officer’s official duties or a person who sends,
29 transmits, distributes or delivers a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot to the
30 voter when permitted pursuant to this title.
31 (b) Deliver to an election board officer in the course of the election board
32 officer’s official duties any ballot other than the one received.
33 (c) Place any mark upon his or her ballot by which it may afterward be
34 identified as the one that he or she voted, other than any such mark that is permitted
35 to be placed on a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of
36 the voter with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
37 3. A person other than a county or city clerk shall not set up a ballot drop box
38 that purports to be an official ballot drop box for mail ballots.
39 4. Any person who violates any provision of this section is guilty of a
40 category E felony and shall be punished as provided in NRS 193.130.
41 Sec. 49. NRS 293.740 is hereby amended to read as follows:
42 293.740 1. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, it is unlawful
43 inside a polling place, within 100 feet from the entrance to the building or other
44 structure in which a polling place is located, inside the area of a county or city jail
45 where a person detained in the jail may vote or within 100 feet from the entrance of
46 the area in a jail where a person detained in the jail may vote:
47 (a) For any person to solicit a vote or speak to a voter on the subject of
48 marking the voter’s ballot [.] unless the person is conducting an exit poll.
49 (b) For any person, including an election board officer, to do any
50 electioneering on election day.
51  The county clerk or registrar of voters shall ensure that, at the outer limits of the
52 area within which electioneering is prohibited, notices are continuously posted on
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 39
1 which are printed in large letters “Distance Marker: No electioneering between this
2 point and the entrance to the polling place.”
3 2. The county clerk shall ensure that any notice posted pursuant to subsection
4 1 is:
5 (a) At least 17 inches by 11 inches in size;
6 (b) Placed on a window or door of the polling place or a freestanding sign; and
7 (c) Visible to a person approaching the outer limits of the area within which
8 electioneering is prohibited pursuant to subsection 1.
9 3. The provisions of subsections 1 and 2 do not apply to the conduct of a
10 person in a private residence or on commercial or residential property that is within
11 100 feet from the entrance to a building or other structure in which a polling place
12 is located. The provisions of subsection 1 are not intended to prohibit a person from
13 voting solely because he or she is wearing a prohibited political insigne and is
14 reasonably unable to remove the insigne or cover it. In such a case, the election
15 board officer shall take such action as is necessary to allow the voter to vote as
16 expediently as possible and then assist the voter in exiting the polling place as soon
17 as is possible.
18 4. Any person who violates any provision of this section is guilty of a gross
19 misdemeanor.
20 5. As used in this section, “electioneering” means campaigning for or against
21 a candidate, ballot question or political party by:
22 (a) Posting signs relating to the support of or opposition to a candidate, ballot
23 question or political party;
24 (b) Distributing literature relating to the support of or opposition to a
25 candidate, ballot question or political party;
26 (c) Using loudspeakers to broadcast information relating to the support of or
27 opposition to a candidate, ballot question or political party;
28 (d) Buying, selling, wearing or displaying any badge, button or other insigne
29 which expressly refers to any political party or a candidate or ballot question to be
30 voted upon at that election; or
31 (e) Soliciting signatures to any kind of petition.

47 Sec. 81. The provisions of NRS 354.599 do not apply to any additional
48 expenses of a local government that are related to the provisions of this act.
49 Sec. 82. 1. This section and section 81 of this act become effective upon
50 passage and approval.
51 2. Sections 1 to 80, inclusive, of this act become effective:
Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 49
1 (a) Upon passage and approval for the purpose of adopting any regulations and
2 performing any other preparatory administrative tasks that are necessary to carry
3 out the provisions of this act; and
4 (b) On July 1, 2025, for all other purposes.

A.B. 534 (§§ 18, 20, 51, 61).

EXPLANATION: Matter in (1) blue bold italics is new language in the original
bill; (2) variations of green bold underlining is language proposed to be added in
this amendment; (3) red strikethrough is deleted language in the original bill; (4)
purple double strikethrough is language proposed to be deleted in this amendment;

retained in this amendment.

A.B. No. 534—Revises provisions relating to elections. (BDR 24-975)

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 3
ASSEMBLY BILL NO. 534–COMMITTEE ON
LEGISLATIVE OPERATIONS AND ELECTIONS
(ON BEHALF OF THE SECRETARY OF STATE)
MARCH 24, 2025
_______________
Referred to Committee on Legislative Operations and Elections
SUMMARY—Revises provisions relating to elections. (BDR 24-975)
FISCAL NOTE: Effect on Local Government: May have Fiscal Impact.
Effect on the State: Yes.
CONTAINS UNFUNDED MANDATE (§§ [2,] 18, 20, [21,] 51, 61)
(NOT REQUESTED BY AFFECTED LOCAL GOVERNMENT)
~
EXPLANATION – Matter in bolded italics is new; matter between brackets [omitted material] is material to be omitted.
AN ACT relating to elections; [requiring the Secretary of State to allow certain
persons detained in jail to use the system of approved electronic
transmission to register to vote and cast a ballot;] revising provisions
relating to voter registration and updating voter registration
information; renaming certain provisional ballots to “conditional
ballots”; revising provisions relating to certain petitions; [revising the
deadline for candidates to file a declaration of candidacy;] revising
provisions relating to the publication of certain information by a
county clerk; [authorizing the Secretary of State to require certain
employees to attend a training course concerning elections
procedures;] revising provisions relating mail ballots; revising
provisions relating to the testing of certain technology prior to an
election; defining the term “personal knowledge” for purposes of
certain challenges; revising provisions relating to risk-limiting audits;
revising provisions relating to certain prohibited conduct in or around a
polling place; revising provisions relating to mechanical voting
systems; authorizing, under certain circumstances, the Secretary of
State to adjust the date of the presidential preference primary election;
making various other changes relating to elections; and providing other
matters properly relating thereto.
Legislative Counsel’s Digest:
1 [Existing law requires the Secretary of State to establish a system of approved electronic
2 transmission through which voters may register to vote and apply for and cast a ballot. (NRS
3 293D.200) Existing law further sets forth provisions governing voting by persons who are
4 detained in a county or city jail. (NRS 293.269971, 293.269973, 293.269975) Section 2 of this

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 4
5 bill requires the Secretary of State to allow: (1) an elector who is detained in a county or city
6 jail to use the system of approved electronic transmission established for covered voters who
7 are overseas or in the military to register to vote; and (2) a registered voter who is detained in
8 a county or city jail to use the system of approved electronic transmission to apply for and cast
9 a ballot in every election where the system of approved electronic transmission is available to
10 a covered voter who is overseas or in the military. Section 15 of this bill requires the Secretary
11 of State to prescribe the procedures to be followed and the requirements of the use of the
12 system of approved electronic transmission by electors and voters who are detained in a
13 county or city jail. Section 21 of this bill requires the report submitted to the Secretary of State
14 by a person who administers a county or city jail concerning elections conducted in such jails
15 to include an explanation of the process the jail used to comply with the provisions of section
16 2. (NRS 293.269975)]
17 Section 3 of this bill requires, with limited exception, a county or city clerk to respond
18 within 2 working days after receiving any request from the Secretary of State for information
19 or data relating to [an] the current election [.] cycle.
20 Section 4 of this bill provides that if an active registered voter moves to another county
21 and registers to vote therein, which may include, without limitation, an application to register
22 to vote which is transmitted to a county clerk from an automatic voter registration agency, it
23 shall be deemed that the voter is updating his or her voter registration rather than registering to
24 vote and, with certain exceptions, the voter must not be required to cast a provisional ballot on
25 the basis of such an update.
26 Existing law sets forth certain procedures governing the use of provisional ballots by
27 registered voters who update their voter registration information after the close of registration
28 for an election and by electors who register to vote in person or by computer during certain
29 periods of time leading up to and during an election. Specifically, existing law: (1) with
30 certain exceptions, requires an elector who is deemed conditionally registered to vote under
31 such circumstances to cast his or her vote by a provisional ballot; and (2) authorizes a county
32 or city clerk, under certain circumstances, to require a registered voter who updates his or her
33 voter registration to cast a provisional ballot in an election. (NRS 293.5772-293.5887)
34 Sections 5, 23, 26, 32 and 38-47 of this bill rename ballots cast under such circumstances to
35 be “conditional ballots.”
36 Existing law requires certain petitions to be submitted to a county clerk for verification of
37 the signatures on the petition and sets forth certain deadlines for such submission. (NRS
38 293.128, 293.172, 293.200, 295.056, 298.109, 306.035, 306.110) Section 65 of this bill
39 [prohibits] authorizes a county clerk, under certain circumstances, to delay beginning
40 verification for petitions for referendum and certain initiatives . [from being submitted to a
41 county clerk earlier than the 13th day following the primary or general election, as
42 appropriate.] (NRS 295.056) Existing law requires, after the submission of certain petitions
43 containing signatures which are required to be verified, the county clerk to determine the
44 number of signatures affixed to the documents and forward that information to the Secretary
45 of State. (NRS 293.1276) Section 6 of this bill increases the time provided to a county clerk to
46 make such a determination: (1) for a petition to place the name of a candidate for partisan
47 office of a minor political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the ballot,
48 from 2 working days to 7 working days; and (2) for any other petition which is required to be
49 submitted for such purposes, from 4 working days to 9 working days.
50 If the Secretary of State finds that the total number of signatures submitted to all the
51 county clerks is 100 percent or more of the number of registered voters needed to declare the
52 petition sufficient, existing law requires: (1) the Secretary of State to immediately notify the
53 county clerks; and (2) each of the county clerks, after the receipt of such notification, to
54 determine the number of registered voters who have signed the document. (NRS 293.1277)
55 Section 7 of this bill increases the time provided to a county clerk to make such a
56 determination: (1) for a petition to recall a public officer who holds a statewide office, from
57 20 working days to 25 working days; (2) for a petition to place the name of a candidate for
58 partisan office of a minor political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the
59 ballot, from 3 working days to 8 working days; and (3) for any other petition which is required
60 to be submitted for such purposes, from 9 working days to 14 working days. Sections 8 and
61 11 of this bill require a petition to place the name of a candidate for partisan office of a minor
62 political party or an independent candidate for partisan office on the ballot be submitted to the

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 5
63 county clerk for verification or filing, respectively, not later than 25 working days, rather
64 than 10 working days, before the last day to file the petition.
65 Existing law [provides] requires that the [period for filing a declaration] petition of
66 candidacy [: (1) for judicial candidates begins on the first Monday in January of the year in
67 which the election is to be held and ends the second Friday after the first Monday in January;
68 and (2) for all nonjudicial candidates begins on] for an independent candidate for partisan
69 office be filed not earlier than the first Monday in March of the year in which the election is
70 to be held and [ends] not later than the [second] third Friday [after the first Monday] in
71 [March. (NRS 293.177, 293C.145, 293C.175) Sections 9-11, 58 and 59 of this bill instead
72 provide that the period for filing a declaration of candidacy for both judicial and nonjudicial
73 candidates begins on the first Monday in February of the year in which the election is to be
74 held and ends not later than 5 p.m. on the second Friday after the first Monday in February.
75 Section 9 similarly revises the dates by which a minor political party is required by existing
76 law to file a list of its candidates for partisan office. (NRS 293.1725)] June. (NRS 293.200)
77 Section 11 [further] instead provides that a petition of candidacy for an independent
78 candidate for partisan office must not be filed earlier than the [first] second Monday [in
79 February rather] after the primary election and not later than the [first Monday in March.]
80 third Friday after the primary election. Section 11 additionally: (1) requires such a
81 petition to be submitted to the county clerk for verification during this period of time;
82 and (2) provides that if such a petition is submitted in a timely manner but the Secretary
83 of State receives certificates from the county clerks showing the petition has met certain
84 requirements after this deadline, the petition is deemed to be timely filed.
85 Existing law requires a county clerk to publish certain information concerning elections
86 in a newspaper of general circulation. (NRS 293.203, 293.253, 293.3073, 293.3576, 293.391,
87 293.464, 298.670) Sections 12, 25, 27, 28, 31 and 68 of this bill instead require the county
88 clerk to publish such notices in such a manner as the county clerk deems proper, which may
89 include, without limitation, publication in a newspaper of general circulation, on the Internet
90 website of the county clerk or on the social media account of the county clerk.
91 Under existing law, the Secretary of State is required to cause to be published in a
92 newspaper of general circulation, on three separate occasions, in each county of the State,
93 together with any explanatory matter to be placed on the ballot, the entire text of a proposed
94 amendment to the Nevada Constitution which is proposed by an initiative petition. (Nev. Art.
95 19, § 2; NRS 293.253) Section 17 of this bill authorizes a county clerk to also publish such
96 materials in any other manner as the county clerk deems proper which may include, without
97 limitation, publication on the Internet website of the county clerk or on the social media
98 account of the county clerk.
99 Existing law requires the Secretary of State to adopt regulations, not inconsistent with the
100 election laws of this State, for the conduct of primary, presidential preference primary,
101 general, special and district elections in all cities and counties. (NRS 293.247) Section 14 of
102 this bill authorizes the Secretary of State to adopt regulations which provide standards for
103 certain reports which are required to be filed by a county or city clerk.
104 [Section 16 of this bill authorizes the Secretary of State to require any deputy or
105 employee of the Office of the Secretary of State whose duties relate to elections to attend the
106 training course provided by the Secretary of State concerning elections procedures. (NRS
107 293.2504)]
108 Existing law authorizes a mail ballot central counting board to begin counting the
109 received mail ballots 15 days before the day of the election and requires the board to complete
110 the count of all mail ballots on or before the seventh day following the election. (NRS
111 293.269931, 293C.26331) Sections 20 and 61 of this bill: (1) require, instead of authorize, the
112 mail ballot central counting board to begin counting the received mail ballots 15 days before
113 the day of the election; and (2) require the mail ballot central counting board to process each
114 mail ballot [on] within 24 hours after receipt of the [day that the] mail ballot unless a
115 waiver is [received. Section] granted by the Secretary of State. Sections 19 and 60 of this
116 bill [requires] require the Secretary of State, rather than a county or city clerk, to establish
117 procedures for minimum requirements for the processing and counting of mail ballots.
118 (NRS [293.269925)] 293.269925, 293C.26325)
119 Existing law requires a county clerk to: (1) prepare and distribute to certain persons in the
120 county a mail ballot for every election; and (2) allow a voter to elect not to receive such a mail
121 ballot by submitting a written notice to the county clerk which must be received by the county

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 6
122 clerk not later than 60 days before the day of the election. (NRS 293.269911) Section 18 of
123 this bill authorizes a voter who elects not to receive a mail ballot to later elect to receive a
124 mail ballot for the election if he or she, not later than 14 days before the election, submits to
125 the county clerk a written notice in the form prescribed by the county clerk. Sections 18 and
126 59.5 of this bill revise the deadline for distributing a mail ballot to each registered voter
127 who resides within the State from not later than 20 days before the election to instead on
128 or after the fifth Monday before the election but not later than the fourth Monday
129 before the election.
130 Existing law authorizes an elector to vote in the county or city in which the elector is
131 eligible to vote by submitting an application to register to vote by computer using the system
132 established by the Secretary of State before the elector appears at a polling place to vote in
133 person. Existing law further requires an elector who submits an application to register to vote
134 in such a manner less than 14 days before the election to vote in person. (NRS 293.5837,
135 293.671) Section 41 of this bill instead requires an elector who submits such an application
136 less than 18 days before the election to vote in person. Section 18 requires a county clerk to
137 prepare and distribute a mail ballot to each person who registers to vote or updates his or her
138 voter registration information not later than 18 days, rather than 14 days, before the election.
139 (NRS 293.269911)
140 Existing law requires a county clerk, if the county clerk uses an electronic roster, to
141 complete a test of the electronic roster not earlier than 2 weeks before and not later than 5 p.m.
142 on the day before the first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance to ensure
143 its functionality. (NRS 293.275) Section 22 of this bill prohibits such a test from being
144 completed earlier than 6 weeks, instead of 2 weeks, before the first day of the period for early
145 voting by personal appearance. Section 55 of this bill similarly revises the time period
146 provided in existing law for a county or city clerk to perform certain tests on a mechanical
147 recording device which directly records votes electronically and any automatic tabulating
148 equipment and programs. (NRS 293B.150)
149 Sections 24 and 33 of this bill define the term “personal knowledge” for purposes of
150 certain provisions of existing law which authorize certain persons to challenge the right of a
151 person to vote and provide that the term does not include knowledge obtained from a third
152 party. (NRS 293.303, 293.535)
153 Existing law requires each county clerk to conduct a risk-limiting audit of the results of
154 an election. (NRS 293.394) Section 29 of this bill renames such audits to “election accuracy
155 audits.” Existing law provides that certain materials used in the completion of logic and
156 accuracy tests must be sealed and deposited in the vaults of the county clerk. (NRS 293B.170)
157 Section 56 of this bill provides that such materials are subject to inspection for the purposes of
158 an election accuracy audit.
159 Section 30 of this bill provides that the term “canvass” as used in certain provisions
160 relating to recounts demanded by a candidate defeated at an election includes, in any general
161 election, the canvass by the Supreme Court of the returns for a candidate for United States
162 Senator or Representative in Congress. (NRS 293.403)
163 Existing law requires a county clerk to cancel the preregistration or registration of a
164 person under certain circumstances and authorizes or requires the reregistration of certain
165 electors whose registration is cancelled. (NRS 293.540, 293.543) Section 34 of this bill
166 requires a county clerk to cancel the preregistration or registration of a person if the county
167 clerk receives, from a person who is within the second degree of consanguinity of the person,
168 a sworn affidavit which indicates the death of the person. Section 35 of this bill requires, if
169 the registration or preregistration of an elector is cancelled under such circumstances and the
170 county clerk later determines that the registration or preregistration should not have been
171 cancelled, the county clerk to reregister or repreregister the elector.
172 Existing law provides that the last day for a person to register to vote for certain elections
173 that are held on the same day as a primary election, presidential preference primary election or
174 general election is, if the person is registering by appearing in person at the office of the
175 county clerk or certain county facilities, the fourth Tuesday preceding the primary election,
176 presidential preference primary election or general election. (NRS 293.560) Section 36 of this
177 bill instead provides that the last day to register to vote in such a manner is the day before the
178 first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance. Section 62 of this bill similarly
179 revises such deadlines for registration for a primary city, general city, recall and special city
180 election if there is a period for early voting for the primary or general city election. Section 37

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 7
181 of this bill requires, if an application to register to vote is received not later than 5 days after
182 the appropriate deadline, a county clerk to accept the application if it is obtained from the
183 Department of Motor Vehicles and is completed by, depending on if there is a period for early
184 voting by personal appearance, the day before the first day of the period for early voting by
185 personal appearance or the last day to register to vote by mail. (NRS 293.5727)
186 Existing law further provides that if a recall or special election is not held on the same
187 day as certain elections, the last day to register to vote for the recall or special election by any
188 method of registration is the third Saturday preceding the recall or special election. (NRS
189 293.560) Section 36 instead provides that the last day to register to vote for such a recall or
190 special election: (1) by mail is the second Tuesday preceding the recall or special election; (2)
191 by appearing in person at the office of the county clerk or certain county facilities is,
192 depending on if there is a period for early voting for the recall or special election, either the
193 day before the first day of the period for early voting by personal appearance or the third
194 Saturday preceding the recall or special election; and (3) by computer using the system
195 established on the Internet website of the Office of the Secretary of State is the day of the
196 recall or special election. Section 62 similarly revises deadlines for such registration for such
197 recall and special city elections.
198 Sections 48 and 49 of this bill exempt a person who is conducting an exit poll from
199 certain provisions of law which prohibit a person from: (1) with certain exceptions, remaining
200 inside or outside of any polling place so as to interfere with the conduct of an election; and (2)
201 in certain locations, soliciting a vote or speaking to a voter on the subject of marking the
202 voter’s ballots. (NRS 293.730, 293.740)
203 Section 50 of this bill provides that the termination of a contract by certain local
204 governing bodies for the lease or use of a mechanical voting system or mechanical recording
205 device which is currently used in any election of this State is provisional unless such an entity:
206 (1) submits to the Secretary of State a plan to transition to a new mechanical voting system or
207 mechanical recording device which is approved by the Secretary of State; and (2) signs a
208 contract for the purchase, lease or use of the new mechanical voting system or mechanical
209 recording device.
210 Existing law authorizes mechanical voting systems to be used to cast, register, record and
211 count ballots or votes at all statewide, county, city and district elections of any kind held in
212 this State. (NRS 293B.050) Section 51 of this bill instead provides that ballots or votes: (1)
213 may be cast, registered and recorded using a mechanical voting system; and (2) must be
214 counted using a mechanical voting system. Sections 13, 52-54, 57, 63, 64, 66 and 69-80 of
215 this bill make conforming changes to require the use of a mechanical voting system for
216 counting votes and clarify that the use of a mechanical voting system for casting ballots is
217 authorized but not required.
218 Section 67 of this bill authorizes the Secretary of State, with the approval of the
219 Legislative Commission, to adjust the date of the presidential primary election which is set
220 forth in existing law as the first Tuesday in February of each presidential election year. (NRS
221 298.650)
THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF NEVADA, REPRESENTED IN
SENATE AND ASSEMBLY, DO ENACT AS FOLLOWS:
1 Section 1. Chapter 293 of NRS is hereby amended by adding thereto the
2 provisions set forth as sections 2, 3 and 4 of this act.
3 Sec. 2. [1. Except as otherwise provided in this section, the Secretary of
4 State shall allow during the period of early voting and on election day:
5 (a) An elector who is detained in a county or city jail to use the system of
6 approved electronic transmission established pursuant to NRS 293D.200 to
7 register to vote in every election where the system of approved electronic
8 transmission is available to a covered voter to register to vote. The deadline for
9 such an elector to use the system of approved electronic transmission to register
10 to vote is the same as the deadline set forth in NRS 293D.230 for a covered voter
11 to register to vote.

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 8
1 (b) A registered voter who is in the custody of a county or city jail to use the
2 system of approved electronic transmission established pursuant to NRS
3 293D.200 to apply for and cast a ballot in every election where the system of
4 approved electronic transmission is available to a covered voter to request and
5 cast a military-overseas ballot. The deadlines for such a registered voter to use
6 the system of approved electronic transmission to request and cast a ballot are the
7 same as the deadlines set forth in NRS 293D.310 and 293D.400 for a covered
8 voter to request and cast a military-overseas ballot.
9 2. Upon receipt of an application and ballot cast by a person pursuant to
10 subsection 1 using the system of approved electronic transmission established
11 pursuant to NRS 293D.200, the local elections official shall affix, mark or

36 established pursuant to NRS 293D.200 unless the jail has the technology that is

39 system of approved electronic transmission shall not prohibit, restrict or monitor
40 the use of the system of approved electronic transmission by a person detained in
41 the jail.
