Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 24
1 2. If a person is challenged, an election board officer shall tender the
2 challenged person the following oath or affirmation:
3 (a) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person does not belong
4 to the political party designated upon the roster, “I swear or affirm under penalty of
5 perjury that I belong to the political party designated upon the roster”;
6 (b) If the challenge is on the ground that the roster does not show that the
7 challenged person designated the political party to which he or she claims to
8 belong, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I designated on the
9 application to register to vote the political party to which I claim to belong”;
10 (c) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person does not reside
11 at the residence for which the address is listed in the roster, “I swear or affirm under
12 penalty of perjury that I reside at the residence for which the address is listed in the
13 roster”;
14 (d) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person previously
15 voted a ballot for the election, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I
16 have not voted for any of the candidates or questions included on this ballot for this
17 election”; or
18 (e) If the challenge is on the ground that the challenged person is not the
19 person he or she claims to be, “I swear or affirm under penalty of perjury that I am
20 the person whose name is in this roster.”
21  The oath or affirmation must be set forth on a form prepared by the Secretary of
22 State and signed by the challenged person under penalty of perjury.
23 3. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 4, if the challenged person
24 refuses to execute the oath or affirmation so tendered, the person must not be issued
25 a ballot, and the election board officer shall indicate in the roster “Challenged” by
26 the person’s name.
27 4. If the challenged person refuses to execute the oath or affirmation set forth
28 in paragraph (a) or (b) of subsection 2, the election board officers shall issue the
29 person a nonpartisan ballot.
30 5. If the challenged person refuses to execute the oath or affirmation set forth
31 in paragraph (c) of subsection 2, the election board officers shall inform the person
32 that he or she is entitled to vote only in the manner prescribed in NRS 293.304.
33 6. If the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation and the challenge
34 is not based on the ground set forth in paragraph (e) of subsection 2, the election
35 board officers shall issue the person a partisan ballot.
36 7. If the challenge is based on the ground set forth in paragraph (c) of
37 subsection 2, and the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation, the
38 election board shall not issue the person a ballot until he or she furnishes
39 satisfactory identification which contains proof of the address at which the person
40 actually resides. For the purposes of this subsection, a voter registration card does
41 not provide proof of the address at which a person resides.
42 8. If the challenge is based on the ground set forth in paragraph (e) of
43 subsection 2 and the challenged person executes the oath or affirmation, the
44 election board shall not issue the person a ballot unless the person:
45 (a) Furnishes official identification which contains a photograph of the person,
46 such as a driver’s license or other official document; or
47 (b) Brings before the election board officers a person who is at least 18 years
48 of age who:
49 (1) Furnishes official identification which contains a photograph of that
50 person, such as a driver’s license or other official document; and
51 (2) Executes an oath or affirmation under penalty of perjury that the
52 challenged person is who he or she swears to be.
53 9. The election board officers shall:

1 (a) Record on the challenge list:
2 (1) The name of the challenged person;
3 (2) The name of the registered voter who initiated the challenge; and
4 (3) The result of the challenge; and

31 2. Unused ballots, enclosed and sealed, must, after canvass of the votes by the

33 preserved for at least the period during which the election may be contested and
34 adjudicated, after which the unused ballots may be destroyed.
35 3. The rosters containing the signatures of those persons who voted in the
36 election and the tally lists deposited with the board of county commissioners are
37 subject to the inspection of any elector who may wish to examine them at any time
38 after their deposit with the county clerk.
39 4. A contestant of an election may inspect all of the material regarding that
40 election which is preserved pursuant to subsection 1 or 2, except the voted ballots
41 and records printed on paper of voted ballots collected pursuant to NRS 293B.400
42 which are deposited with the county clerk.
43 5. The voted ballots and records printed on paper of voted ballots collected
44 pursuant to NRS 293B.400 which are deposited with the county clerk are not
45 subject to the inspection of anyone, except in cases of a contested election, and then
46 only by the judge, body or board before whom the election is being contested, or by
47 the parties to the contest, jointly, pursuant to an order of such judge, body or board.

23 certification by the county clerk or city clerk of the abstract of votes, the voter:
24 (a) Files in writing a demand with:

26 question affecting more than one county; or

30 whom the demand was made.

32 whom the advance is deposited based on regulations adopted by the Secretary of
33 State defining the term “costs.”
34 4. As used in this section, “canvass” means:
35 (a) In any primary election, the canvass by the board of county commissioners

38 returns for a candidate or ballot question voted for in more than one county.
39 (b) In any primary city election, the canvass by the city council of the returns
40 for a candidate or ballot question voted for in the city.
41 (c) In any general election:
42 (1) The canvass by the Supreme Court of the returns for a candidate for

44 statewide ballot question; or

30 county or city clerk pursuant to this paragraph. The county or city clerk shall
31 authorize at least one of the following methods for a person to register to vote
32 pursuant to this paragraph:
33 (1) A paper application; or
34 (2) The system established by the Secretary of State pursuant to NRS
35 293.671.
36  If the county or city clerk authorizes the use of both methods, the county or city
37 clerk may limit the use of one method to circumstances when the other method is
38 not reasonably available.
39 (c) Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, provide his or her current and
40 valid driver’s license or identification card issued by the Department of Motor
41 Vehicles which shows his or her physical address as proof of the elector’s identity
42 and residency.
43 3. If the driver’s license or identification card issued by the Department of
44 Motor Vehicles to the elector does not have the elector’s current residential address,
45 the following documents may be used to establish the residency of the elector if the
46 current residential address of the elector, as indicated on his or her application to
47 register to vote, is displayed on the document:
48 (a) A military identification card;
49 (b) A utility bill, including, without limitation, a bill for electric, gas, oil, water,
50 sewer, septic, telephone, cellular telephone or cable television service;
51 (c) A bank or credit union statement;
52 (d) A paycheck;
53 (e) An income tax return;

Assembly Amendment No. 909 to Assembly Bill No. 534 Page 36
1 (f) A statement concerning the mortgage, rental or lease of a residence;
2 (g) A motor vehicle registration;
3 (h) A property tax statement; or
4 (i) Any other document issued by a governmental agency.
5 4. Subject to final verification, if an elector registers to vote in person at a
6 polling place pursuant to this section:
7 (a) The elector shall be deemed to be conditionally registered to vote at the
8 polling place upon:
9 (1) The determination that the application to register to vote is complete;
10 and
11 (2) The verification of the elector’s identity and residency pursuant to this
12 section.
13 (b) After the elector is deemed to be conditionally registered to vote at the
14 polling place pursuant to paragraph (a), the elector:
15 (1) May vote in the election only at that polling place;
16 (2) Must vote as soon as practicable and before leaving that polling place;
17 and
18 (3) Must vote by casting a [provisional] conditional ballot, unless it is
19 verified, at that time, that the elector is qualified to register to vote and to cast a
20 regular ballot in the election at that polling place.

3 Sec. 48. NRS 293.730 is hereby amended to read as follows:
4 293.730 1. Except for an election board officer in the course of the election
5 board officer’s official duties, a person shall not:
6 (a) Remain in or outside of any polling place so as to interfere with the conduct
7 of the election. The provisions of this paragraph do not prohibit a person from
8 conducting an exit poll in or outside of the polling place.
9 (b) Accept from any voter a ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter, other
10 than a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter
11 with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
12 (c) Remove a ballot from any polling place before the closing of the polls.
13 (d) Apply for or receive a ballot at any election precinct or district other than
14 one at which the person is entitled to vote.
15 (e) Show his or her ballot to another person, after voting, so as to reveal any of
16 his or her votes on the ballot, other than on his or her mail ballot or military-
17 overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the voter with his or her authorization
18 pursuant to this title.
19 (f) Inside a polling place, ask another person for his or her name, address or
20 political affiliation or for whom he or she intends to vote.
21 (g) Send, transmit, distribute or deliver a ballot to a voter, other than a mail
22 ballot or military-overseas ballot when permitted pursuant to this title.
23 (h) Except when permitted by the voter, alter, change, deface, damage or
24 destroy a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of the
25 voter with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
26 2. A voter shall not:
27 (a) Accept a ballot from another person, other than an election board officer in
28 the course of the election board officer’s official duties or a person who sends,
29 transmits, distributes or delivers a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot to the
30 voter when permitted pursuant to this title.
31 (b) Deliver to an election board officer in the course of the election board
32 officer’s official duties any ballot other than the one received.
33 (c) Place any mark upon his or her ballot by which it may afterward be
34 identified as the one that he or she voted, other than any such mark that is permitted
35 to be placed on a mail ballot or military-overseas ballot prepared by or on behalf of
36 the voter with his or her authorization pursuant to this title.
37 3. A person other than a county or city clerk shall not set up a ballot drop box
38 that purports to be an official ballot drop box for mail ballots.

20 5. As used in this section, “electioneering” means campaigning for or against

23 question or political party;

25 candidate, ballot question or political party;
26 (c) Using loudspeakers to broadcast information relating to the support of or
27 opposition to a candidate, ballot question or political party;

19 forth in subsection 1, will be closed.
20 4. A municipal facility designated pursuant to NRS 293C.520 may be open
21 during the periods described in this section for such hours of operation as the city
22 clerk may determine, as set forth in subsection 3 of NRS 293C.520.
23 Sec. 63. NRS 293C.600 is hereby amended to read as follows:
24 293C.600 1. Before any election where a mechanical voting system will be
25 used [,] for casting ballots, the city clerk shall prepare or cause to be prepared a
26 computer program on cards, tape or other material suitable for use with the
27 computer or counting device to be employed for counting the votes cast. The
28 program must cause the computer or counting device to operate in the following
29 manner:
30 (a) All lawful votes cast by each voter must be counted.
31 (b) All unlawful votes, including, but not limited to, overvotes must not be
32 counted.
33 (c) The computer or counting device must halt or indicate by appropriate signal
34 if a ballot is encountered that lacks a code identifying the precinct in which it was
35 voted.
36 2. The program must be prepared under the supervision of the accuracy
37 certification board appointed pursuant to the provisions of NRS 293B.140.
38 3. The city clerk shall take such measures as he or she deems necessary to
39 protect the program from being altered or damaged.
40 Sec. 64. NRS 295.045 is hereby amended to read as follows:
41 295.045 1. A petition for referendum must be filed with the Secretary of
42 State not less than 120 days before the date of the next succeeding general election.
43 2. The Secretary of State shall certify the questions to the county clerks.
44 3. The title of the statute or resolution must be set out on the ballot, and the
45 question printed upon the ballot for the information of the voters must be as
46 follows: “Shall the statute (setting out its title) be approved?”
47 4. Where a mechanical voting system is used [,] for casting ballots, the title
48 of the statute must appear on the list of offices and candidates and the statements of
49 measures to be voted on and may be condensed to no more than 25 words.
50 5. The votes cast upon the question must be counted and canvassed as the
51 votes for state officers are counted and canvassed.

1 Sec. 65. NRS 295.056 is hereby amended to read as follows:
2 295.056 1. Before a petition for initiative or referendum is filed with the
3 Secretary of State, the petitioners must submit to each county clerk for verification
4 pursuant to NRS 293.1276 to 293.1279, inclusive, the document or documents
5 which were circulated for signature within the clerk’s county. The clerks shall give
6 the person submitting a document or documents a receipt stating the number of
7 documents and pages and the person’s statement of the number of signatures
8 contained therein.
9 2. If a petition for initiative proposes a statute or an amendment to a statute,
10 the document or documents must be submitted not [earlier than the 13th day and
11 not] later than the 15th day following the general election.
12 3. If a petition for initiative proposes an amendment to the Constitution, the
13 document or documents must be submitted not [earlier than the 13th day and not]
14 later than the 15th day following the primary election.
15 4. If the petition is for referendum, the document or documents must be
16 submitted not [earlier than the 13th day and not] later than the 15th day following
17 the primary election.
18 5. All documents which are submitted to a county clerk for verification must
19 be submitted at the same time. If documents concerning the same petition are
20 submitted for verification to more than one county clerk, the documents must be
21 submitted to each county clerk on the same day. At the time that the petition is
22 submitted to a county clerk for verification, the petitioners may designate a contact
23 person who is authorized by the petitioners to address questions or issues relating to
24 the petition.
25 6. A county clerk may delay beginning verification pursuant NRS 293.1276
26 to 293.1279, inclusive:
27 (a) If the petition is a petition for referendum or is a petition for initiative
28 that proposes an amendment to the Constitution, on or after the second Friday
29 before the period for early voting for a primary election. If a county clerk delays
30 verification pursuant to this paragraph, the county clerk must begin verification
31 not later than the 15th day following the primary election.
32 (b) If the petition is a petition for initiative that proposes a statute or an
33 amendment to a statute, on or after the second Friday before the period for early
34 voting for a general election. If a county clerk delays verification pursuant to this
35 paragraph, the county clerk must begin verification not later than the 15th day
36 following the general election.
37 Sec. 66. NRS 295.170 is hereby amended to read as follows:
38 295.170 1. The subject matter of such questions must be stated concisely on
39 the ballot, and the question printed upon the ballot for the information of the voter
40 must be as follows: “Shall the act (setting out the title thereof) be approved?”
41 2. Where a mechanical voting system is used [,] for casting ballots, the title
42 of the act must appear on the list of offices and candidates and the statements of
43 measures to be voted on and may be condensed by the district attorney to 20 words.
44 3. The district attorney shall prepare an explanation of each such question,
45 which must be placed on the ballot or the list of offices and candidates and the
46 statements of measures to be voted on, or posted in the polling place.
47 4. The votes cast upon such question must be counted and canvassed as the
48 votes for county officers are counted and canvassed.
